## Section 001: Github Context Capture Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that The seed title names context capture but does not define repository context as separate content, chronology, and relationship surfaces or explain the preflight-scope-collect-preserve-synthesize workflow.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because GitHub history is distributed across commits, PRs, issues, review threads, commit comments, timeline events, and Discussions, so a single command or flattened transcript can omit the evidence that explains a change.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It becomes blocked by broken authentication or unknown repository identity and becomes misleading when permissions, pagination caps, disabled Discussions, or nested-reply truncation are hidden.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: Assume authorized read access only, never expose credentials, and do not claim complete history beyond the recorded scope, permissions, cursors, and capture time.
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Turn the title section into a mode-selection and collection state machine with bounded, blocked, and raw-artifact reuse branches.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Repository context capture is an evidence-preserving join across heterogeneous surfaces, not a search or summarization task; recoverability matters because synthesis can change without recollecting data.
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to Confirm GHCLI availability, active authentication, host, repository, and capabilities; choose Repo Survey or Artifact Trace with an explicit scope; select the canonical REST, GraphQL, or high-level command per surface; save raw JSON; then render a digest that names chronology, links, gaps, and limits.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because GitHub history is distributed across commits, PRs, issues, review threads, commit comments, timeline events, and Discussions, so a single command or flattened transcript can omit the evidence that explains a change.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; It becomes blocked by broken authentication or unknown repository identity and becomes misleading when permissions, pagination caps, disabled Discussions, or nested-reply truncation are hidden.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: Assume authorized read access only, never expose credentials, and do not claim complete history beyond the recorded scope, permissions, cursors, and capture time.
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: Turn the title section into a mode-selection and collection state machine with bounded, blocked, and raw-artifact reuse branches.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies Repository context capture is an evidence-preserving join across heterogeneous surfaces, not a search or summarization task; recoverability matters because synthesis can change without recollecting data.

- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because GitHub history is distributed across commits, PRs, issues, review threads, commit comments, timeline events, and Discussions, so a single command or flattened transcript can omit the evidence that explains a change.

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: It becomes blocked by broken authentication or unknown repository identity and becomes misleading when permissions, pagination caps, disabled Discussions, or nested-reply truncation are hidden.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are One-command mythology, search-as-archive, comment flattening, unlimited pagination, repo-wide timeline crawling, mutation by default, and HTML scraping are the dominant hazards.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where This default works for onboarding, design archaeology, regression tracing, incident review, and commit-to-decision reconstruction when repository access and scope are known.

- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Github Context Capture Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: Narrow to one PR, issue, commit, or discussion; run a bounded survey before widening; synthesize from previously saved raw JSON; report inaccessible surfaces; or ask the user to restore authentication.

- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because The local context strategy is explicitly progressive, and direct command/API guidance is more relevant to capture fidelity than generic automation material.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It fails when all local files are loaded reflexively, three public URLs are treated as current proof, or workflow automation guidance is used to justify API completeness.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: No new browsing occurred, and public pointers cannot override local read-only, bounded-first, or provenance requirements.
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Retain all rows while adding progressive-loading, relevance, retrieval-state, evidence-date, and invalidation interpretation.

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that The seed offers one repository-generation command, which cannot prove GHCLI auth, repository identity, surface coverage, pagination, comment separation, raw persistence, or digest provenance.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Document structure, collection completeness, and synthesis correctness are separate claims with different evidence.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It fails when one PASS substitutes for API coverage, when rate-limit or permission errors are ignored, or when a digest is reviewed without raw payloads.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: The retained archive command proves only generated-reference properties and cannot validate GitHub data.
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Keep the seed command as one layer and add live/fixture collection, surface, pagination, raw, digest, and safety gates.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Verification should replay synthesis from saved raw JSON; that proves recoverability and separates renderer defects from collection defects.

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that The seed triggers generically on theme or paths and omits the three explicit modes, preflight stop, bounded-first rule, and read-only scope.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Mode selection prevents a narrow question from causing an expensive crawl and prevents a broad question from relying on a single artifact view.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It is blocked by failed auth, unknown host or repo, missing permissions, or a mutation request that has not been explicitly authorized.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: Do not mutate GitHub state or expand collection breadth without explicit user authorization.
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Replace generic bullets with preflight plus Survey, Trace, Digest, widen, and blocked branches.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Mode choice is the first context budget: it determines which evidence can enter the digest and which omissions must be declared.
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to Use Repo Survey for broad evolution, Artifact Trace for one commit, PR, issue, or discussion, and Digest Mode to render a reusable summary from captured data; always preflight and choose scope before querying.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Mode selection prevents a narrow question from causing an expensive crawl and prevents a broad question from relying on a single artifact view.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; It is blocked by failed auth, unknown host or repo, missing permissions, or a mutation request that has not been explicitly authorized.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: Do not mutate GitHub state or expand collection breadth without explicit user authorization.

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that The seed's Adopt, Adapt, Avoid, and Cost rows are generic and do not address survey versus trace, bounded versus exhaustive collection, high-level commands versus API harvesting, or fresh capture versus raw-data reuse.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Each mode trades breadth, detail, network cost, and completeness differently, so no single command is a safe universal default.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It fails when bounded data is called exhaustive, exhaustive capture ignores rate limits, or quick views are persisted as durable archives.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: Mode selection never relaxes read-only safety, provenance, or gap disclosure.
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Replace generic rows with capture-mode, command-surface, breadth, and raw-reuse decisions.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Collection should maximize explanatory value per queried surface, not raw object count.
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to Choose a bounded Repo Survey for orientation, Artifact Trace for a known focal item, exhaustive canonical pagination only when explicitly required, high-level `gh` views for quick reads, API harvesting for durable lists, GraphQL for Discussions, and digest-only replay when raw data is adequate.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Each mode trades breadth, detail, network cost, and completeness differently, so no single command is a safe universal default.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; It fails when bounded data is called exhaustive, exhaustive capture ignores rate limits, or quick views are persisted as durable archives.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: Mode selection never relaxes read-only safety, provenance, or gap disclosure.
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: Replace generic rows with capture-mode, command-surface, breadth, and raw-reuse decisions.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies Collection should maximize explanatory value per queried surface, not raw object count.
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: It fails when bounded data is called exhaustive, exhaustive capture ignores rate limits, or quick views are persisted as durable archives.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are The middle path can combine incomplete data with high cost, and sunk collection effort can pressure the digest to overclaim.

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that The seed gives one stale-evidence retry and generic checkpoints but does not distinguish auth, rate-limit, pagination, GraphQL, endpoint, raw, or digest failures.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Targeted retries avoid duplicate network work, rate-limit pressure, and narrative drift while preserving recoverability.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It is wrong for prohibited access, missing user scope, repeated permission denial, unbounded pagination, mutation side effects, or evidence that cannot be obtained through authorized surfaces.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: Retries cannot bypass permissions, fabricate absent objects, mutate state, or broaden scope without consent.
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Add stage-specific idempotent retries, cursor safety, raw preservation, information-gain checks, and stop paths.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Backpressure preserves a truthful capture boundary by making missing data cheaper to admit than to conceal through repeated calls.

- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to Classify the failed stage, preserve successful raw artifacts, change one relevant condition, retry the smallest idempotent read, compare results, and stop when no new evidence appears or authorization is missing.

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that The seed records sources, proof, generic percentiles, tool calls, delegated tasks, retries, and compact evidence but omits host, repo, mode, surfaces, endpoints, cursors, page caps, raw hashes, relationships, and gap-linked claims.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because A reproducible manifest distinguishes data collection state from interpretation and lets failures resume at the smallest safe point.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It fails when logs contain only the digest, raw terminal dumps hide boundaries, or tokens and private payloads exceed the authorized report.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: Never log credentials or distribute private raw content beyond authorized recipients.
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Convert the generic checklist into a capture-manifest event schema and replay test.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Observability converts an interrupted crawl into a resumable data pipeline rather than an opaque terminal session.
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to Record capture ID, time, host, repository, auth status without token material, mode, scope, filters, capabilities, surfaces, endpoints, pages and cursors, rate limits, raw paths and hashes, relationship links, renderer version, digest path, gaps, retries, and mutation count.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because A reproducible manifest distinguishes data collection state from interpretation and lets failures resume at the smallest safe point.

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that The seed names multiple systems, ownership boundaries, unbounded discovery, production traffic, context drift, and graph narrowing but does not define repository, host, surface, or manifest decomposition.
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because Parallel reads can scale canonical collection, but chronology and relationship synthesis require consistent identities and one adjudicated narrative.
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: It fails across organization-wide joins, mixed hosts, shared cursors, tightly coupled artifacts, or multiple writers racing one manifest and digest.
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: Distributed work remains read-only and cannot merge private data into an output unauthorized for all sources.
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to Add repository, host, surface, manifest, rate-limit, ownership, and merge boundaries.
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Scale is reached when relationship reconciliation and permission asymmetry grow faster than evidence gained from another parallel request.
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because Parallel reads can scale canonical collection, but chronology and relationship synthesis require consistent identities and one adjudicated narrative.

### Question 03: When does the default work well?

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: It fails across organization-wide joins, mixed hosts, shared cursors, tightly coupled artifacts, or multiple writers racing one manifest and digest.
